<div id="review_123644256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123644256" />
    <a title="Laurel Young" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3137295-laurel-young"><img alt="Laurel Young" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500435810p2/3137295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123644256?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel Young" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel Young" href="/user/show/3137295-laurel-young">Laurel Young</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3137295-laurel-young?shelf=my-year-of-agatha">my-year-of-agatha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123644256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14755637956354432058">I love the fact that Agatha Christie was always experimenting with new ways of writing mysteries, rather than resting on her considerable laurels. By 1927 she had already written such masterpieces as The Murder of Roger Ackroyd, so I have no doubt that The Big Four was an intentional departure from her previous work. Unfortunately, it is not one of her more successful efforts. An adventure story doesn't play to her strengths at all. The Big Four is one cliche after another, with Poirot and Hasti</span>
  <span id="freeText14755637956354432058" style="display:none">I love the fact that Agatha Christie was always experimenting with new ways of writing mysteries, rather than resting on her considerable laurels. By 1927 she had already written such masterpieces as The Murder of Roger Ackroyd, so I have no doubt that The Big Four was an intentional departure from her previous work. Unfortunately, it is not one of her more successful efforts. An adventure story doesn't play to her strengths at all. The Big Four is one cliche after another, with Poirot and Hastings constantly cheating death at the hands of one or the other of the nefarious super-villains bent on world domination. The Big Four even have a super-secret underground villains' lair! It's just *silly*, a word I would never associate with Dame Agatha. Perhaps she meant it to be light-hearted fun, but, if so, this does not come through--one usually knows when she is being light-hearted, as with Partners in Crime.<br /><br />It's ironic to me that Agatha keeps me spellbound with her more cerebral, less "active" novels, such as Cards on the Table, but bores me silly when she goes for derring-do. She usually outwits me and I have no problem admitting it, but here I was always a step ahead of the plot. Perhaps this just isn't my cup of tea and The Big Four would be an enjoyable novel for a fan of the adventure genre. I simply am not such a fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14755637956354432058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1223203501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223203501" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223203501?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=1900s-1950s">1900s-1950s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=anglophilia">anglophilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=murder-most-foul">murder-most-foul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223203501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6473927617587945637">At first listening to this audiobook, I was enjoying myself quite a bit. Poirot was there, Hastings was there, back from Brazil, and aren’t we all having a good time now that this mysterious man has shown up in the bedroom, and then expired. Except pretty quickly after that, I realized in fact that the book was not good, and I was not enjoying myself, and even though I did listen to the whole thing in its entirety, I did not *listen* to the book in its entirety. (Quick note: Hugh Fraser remains </span>
  <span id="freeText6473927617587945637" style="display:none">At first listening to this audiobook, I was enjoying myself quite a bit. Poirot was there, Hastings was there, back from Brazil, and aren’t we all having a good time now that this mysterious man has shown up in the bedroom, and then expired. Except pretty quickly after that, I realized in fact that the book was not good, and I was not enjoying myself, and even though I did listen to the whole thing in its entirety, I did not *listen* to the book in its entirety. (Quick note: Hugh Fraser remains a great Christie narrator, I always love when he pops up.)<br /><br />Some things I learned after reading this book: It’s not a true mystery or crime novel, it’s not widely liked (most people dislike it), and it was actually created from a series of short stories that Christie had already published, edited and turned into one “storyline”. Spoiler alert: you can tell. The various episodes in this book read like they have been strung together.<br /><br />What I wanted when I started this book, what I was very much in the mood for, was a classic Christie whodunit, and Poirot using his little grey cells to catch a murderer, while I tried in vain to figure it out. This was not that. This was Poirot going from one crime to the next, sometimes with Hastings and sometimes without him, chasing after four supposed criminal masterminds. There was nothing to figure out, and no throughline of one single crime to hold it all together. I did not care in the least. I’ve heard that Christie doesn’t do thrillers or espionage very well, and now having read this, I find myself seeing where that opinion comes from. Hopefully will be reading a real whodunit from her soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6473927617587945637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3132350710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3132350710" />
    <a title="Mary ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37766180-mary"><img alt="Mary ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555156334p2/37766180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3132350710?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ♥" href="/user/show/37766180-mary">Mary ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3132350710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4391650189946200827">3.5/5 stars<br/><br/><b> If one man does not make a move, the other must, and by permitting the adversary to make the attack one learns something about him. </b><br/><br/>I will be honest with you. I had far higher expectations for this story, considering it is Agatha Christie we are talking about. I was expecting a cleverly plotted mystery like in the Seven Dials, but instead found myself reading something that resembled a "badly made" spy movie with conspiracies about world domination and repeated plotlines. A lot of ti</span>
  <span id="freeText4391650189946200827" style="display:none">3.5/5 stars<br /><br /><b> If one man does not make a move, the other must, and by permitting the adversary to make the attack one learns something about him. </b><br /><br />I will be honest with you. I had far higher expectations for this story, considering it is Agatha Christie we are talking about. I was expecting a cleverly plotted mystery like in the Seven Dials, but instead found myself reading something that resembled a "badly made" spy movie with conspiracies about world domination and repeated plotlines. A lot of times, the story took turns I expected, and I found myself thinking some of the things that happened were very far-fetched. The main character, Hastings, was also not my favourite.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the writing though, as well as the last pages and last twist, and Poirot's and Hastings' friendship made me smile a lot of times while reading. I believe a lot of what happened was based upon luck and speculations, and not so much on careful observation, as Poirot usually solves the mysteries. The little details and ways of murder Christie thought of never fail to surprise me, so I really enjoyed that aspect of the story, especially considering she had a lot of murders to come up with in this one.<br /><br />I also thought the villains were quite "ignorant", despite being so powerful, but I really liked the attitude and backstory of one of them (I am not going to spoil). I also liked the roadtrip plot point as well as the kidnapping plot point, because these always cause some emotional turmoil and anticipation for something to happen. In general, learning that Christie was going through a really tough period in her life while writing this, I can excuse her. Besides, it still remains an enjoyable read, despite the predictability and repetition.<br /><br />Overall, I am really excited to pick up more than her because she truly is the queen of crime fiction ♥ Until the next review, keep being your awesome selves ♥<br />~Mary ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="4391650189946200827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3523082114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3523082114" />
    <a title="Jack Heath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70983025-jack-heath"><img alt="Jack Heath" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3523082114?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Heath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Heath" href="/user/show/70983025-jack-heath">Jack Heath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70983025-jack-heath?shelf=other-j-characters">other-j-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70983025-jack-heath?shelf=other-m-following">other-m-following</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70983025-jack-heath?shelf=category-f-mystery">category-f-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70983025-jack-heath?shelf=other-l-fifty">other-l-fifty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3523082114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10145549202195118006">2 Stars. Rarely have I not reveled in a Christie novel featuring Hercule Poirot. This one was unstructured, tied together loosely, and most importantly, the premise was totally unfeasible! As explained by Poirot, an international conspiracy lead by four extraordinary villains is planning world domination, and he and Hastings must stop them. He asserts, "From their (secret) headquarters, the leaders of the organization will issue by wireless their orders to their followers who are numbered by tho</span>
  <span id="freeText10145549202195118006" style="display:none">2 Stars. Rarely have I not reveled in a Christie novel featuring Hercule Poirot. This one was unstructured, tied together loosely, and most importantly, the premise was totally unfeasible! As explained by Poirot, an international conspiracy lead by four extraordinary villains is planning world domination, and he and Hastings must stop them. He asserts, "From their (secret) headquarters, the leaders of the organization will issue by wireless their orders to their followers who are numbered by thousands in every country, (and ..) the dictators of the world will emerge." I was incredulous that such a rational intellect as Poirot could be made to espouse such stupidity. It reminded me of the craziness of new world order conspiracy theories such as the Illuminati, or Jewish infiltration of western governments, or the threat of Freemasonry. Only after reading did I discover what Christie had done. She tied together 12 short stories, which first appeared in "Sketch" in 1924, into a themed book in 1927. A mish-mash which didn't work. But some of the short mysteries are tantalizing; I will seek them out and report back! (September 2020)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10145549202195118006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2431873-emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2754395997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10816692778533301940">This book is batshit insane and thus, very enjoyable. I would recommend that you read this only if you have read all other Poirot books, because reading <i>The Big Four</i> will give you the mistaken impression that Poirot is a James Bond-style detective who works on an international scale to bring down sinister cabals of criminals. As we all know, Poirot primarily shines when he is placed in an English country house closed-circle mystery, not when he is busy faking his own death and sending Hastings u</span>
  <span id="freeText10816692778533301940" style="display:none">This book is batshit insane and thus, very enjoyable. I would recommend that you read this only if you have read all other Poirot books, because reading <i>The Big Four</i> will give you the mistaken impression that Poirot is a James Bond-style detective who works on an international scale to bring down sinister cabals of criminals. As we all know, Poirot primarily shines when he is placed in an English country house closed-circle mystery, not when he is busy faking his own death and sending Hastings undercover. So this book is ridiculous, and that's what makes it fun for any longtime Christie reader. Where else are you going to see the rise of Achille Poirot? (He raises the rating of this book by an entire star on his own.)</span>

  <span id="freeText13697232721810322196" style="display:none">Christie goes down a James Bond-esque route with a sinister international organisation aiming at world domination and with an all-powerful death ray at their disposal - luckily, though, we have Hastings and Poirot in our corner who, with no more than ze little grey cells, a sprinkling of aniseed on the shoes (so that bloodhounds can track them, you see) and some up-and-at-'em attitude manage to foil every dastardly plot and restore world peace - phew!<br /><br />So... not one of Christie's best though there are some little gems of plotlines here: the death of the chess master is one of my favourites. Lucky for us Dame Agatha realised that detection is her forté rather than thriller writing.</span>

<div id="review_2827300715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2827300715" />
    <a title="Gayathri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8118494-gayathri"><img alt="Gayathri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504259628p2/8118494.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gayathri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gayathri" href="/user/show/8118494-gayathri">Gayathri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8118494-gayathri?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8118494-gayathri?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8118494-gayathri?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8118494-gayathri?shelf=classicsnchristieclub">classicsnchristieclub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8118494-gayathri?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2827300715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17960934064291237234">Read the full review at <a href='https://elgeewrites.com/book-review-big-four-agatha-christie-spy/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elgee Writes</a><br/><br/>My initial thoughts<br/>The Classics N Christie has been reading Agatha Christie’s books based on the publication dates. This has been very helpful for me to understand the different writing and story telling styles that the author has been trying. I wish I could The Big Four is one of those attempts, that kinda bombed for me. <br/><br/>Earlier in the Murder on the Links, Dame Christie tried her hand at romance in mystery novels which I didn’t enjoy much. I enjoyed her take </span>
  <span id="freeText17960934064291237234" style="display:none">Read the full review at <a href="https://elgeewrites.com/book-review-big-four-agatha-christie-spy/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Elgee Writes</a><br /><br />My initial thoughts<br />The Classics N Christie has been reading Agatha Christie’s books based on the publication dates. This has been very helpful for me to understand the different writing and story telling styles that the author has been trying. I wish I could The Big Four is one of those attempts, that kinda bombed for me. <br /><br />Earlier in the Murder on the Links, Dame Christie tried her hand at romance in mystery novels which I didn’t enjoy much. I enjoyed her take on spy thriller even lesser. I just can’t wait to get back to cozy little town mysteries from her. <br /><br />Things that worked for me<br /><br />The Big Four reminded me a lot of Sherlock vs Moriarty (I love that).<br />It may work better if you pick the book when you are in the mood to read a spy thriller. <br /><br />Things that didn’t work for me<br /><br />The Big Four seemed like a bundle of short mysteries badly woven together, which I found out to be true later. The Big Four was indeed published as a twelve short mysteries during a particularly bad time of Christie personally.<br />There are too many named characters and most of them do not even reappear after a scene or two.<br />I don’t like how Poirot somehow turned into James Bond at the end of the book. That is so not our Belgian detective. <br /><br />Bottom-line<br />If you are looking to read a typical Christie or Poirot’s mystery you will be disappointed. I never thought I would read Christie’s book that would disappoint me as much, but here it is. <br /><br /><a href="https://elgeewrites.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/elgeewrites" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/elgeewrites" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.amazon.in/gp/profile/amzn1.account.AHHNMWLTU24FLIQ2ZKFJXAWCB42Q?ref_=cm_cr_srp_d_pdp&amp;" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Amazon</a> |</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LTr5XL6ahQ7X85b7SdeKNTQkcQGj/o1bJt+eOT2NNnpmdXSskewuI6EijsLuQYVjsbVU/Fy2PGLrsXPbrVUkYA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D/qHuf4slF16cDTPpfYt/vSFfPxOPi0LkEB8AixHecpEtQpJ0Vo/cAyhLPYCYCKocRRZAbF2nDJdLpHgvJ9r0A==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">About Agatha Christie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1589991473p3/123715.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">Agatha Christie
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
42,807
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12359988023329765706"><i>Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16273767.Mary_Westmacott' title='Mary Westmacott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary Westmacott</a></b>, and was occasionally published under the name <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19960421.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan' title='Agatha Christie Mallowan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie Mallowan</a></b>.</i><br/><br/>Agatha Christie is the best-selling author of all time. She wrote 66 crime novels and story collections, fourteen plays, and six novels under a pseudonym in Romance. Her books have sold over a billion copies in the English language and a billion in t</span>
  <span id="freeText12359988023329765706" style="display:none"><i>Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16273767.Mary_Westmacott" title="Mary Westmacott" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Westmacott</a></b>, and was occasionally published under the name <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19960421.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan" title="Agatha Christie Mallowan" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie Mallowan</a></b>.</i><br /><br />Agatha Christie is the best-selling author of all time. She wrote 66 crime novels and story collections, fourteen plays, and six novels under a pseudonym in Romance. Her books have sold over a billion copies in the English language and a billion in translation. According to Index Translationum, she remains the most-translated individual author, having been translated into at least 103 languages. She is the creator of two of the most enduring figures in crime literature-Hercule Poirot and Miss Jane Marple-and author of <i>The Mousetrap</i>, the longest-running play in the history of modern theatre. <br /><br />Agatha Mary Clarissa Miller was born in Torquay, Devon, England, U.K., as the youngest of three. The Millers had two other children: Margaret Frary Miller (1879–1950), called Madge, who was eleven years Agatha's senior, and Louis Montant Miller (1880–1929), called Monty, ten years older than Agatha. <br /><br />Before marrying and starting a family in London, she had served in a Devon hospital during the First World War, tending to troops coming back from the trenches. During the First World War, she worked at a hospital as a nurse; later working at a hospital pharmacy, a job that influenced her work, as many of the murders in her books are carried out with poison. During the Second World War, she worked as a pharmacy assistant at University College Hospital, London, acquiring a good knowledge of poisons which feature in many of her novels.<br /><br />Her first novel, <i>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</i>, came out in 1920. During her first marriage, Agatha published six novels, a collection of short stories, and a number of short stories in magazines.<br /><br />In late 1926, Agatha's husband, Archie, revealed that he was in love with another woman, Nancy Neele, and wanted a divorce. On 8 December 1926 the couple quarreled, and Archie Christie left their house, Styles, in Sunningdale, Berkshire, to spend the weekend with his mistress at Godalming, Surrey. That same evening Agatha disappeared from her home, leaving behind a letter for her secretary saying that she was going to Yorkshire. Her disappearance caused an outcry from the public, many of whom were admirers of her novels. Despite a massive manhunt, she was not found for eleven days.<br /><br />In 1930, Christie married archaeologist Max Mallowan (Sir Max from 1968) after joining him in an archaeological dig. Their marriage was especially happy in the early years and remained so until Christie's death in 1976.<br /><br />Christie frequently used familiar settings for her stories. Christie's travels with Mallowan contributed background to several of her novels set in the Middle East. Other novels (such as <i>And Then There Were None</i>) were set in and around Torquay, where she was born. Christie's 1934 novel <i>Murder on the Orient Express</i> was written in the Hotel Pera Palace in Istanbul, Turkey, the southern terminus of the railway. The hotel maintains Christie's room as a memorial to the author. The Greenway Estate in Devon, acquired by the couple as a summer residence in 1938, is now in the care of the National Trust.<br /><br />Christie often stayed at Abney Hall in Cheshire, which was owned by her brother-in-law, James Watts. She based at least two of her stories on the hall: the short story <i>The Adventure of the Christmas Pudding</i>, and the novel <i>After the Funeral</i>. Abney Hall became Agatha's greatest inspiration for country-house life, with all the servants and grandeur which have been woven into her plots.<br /><br /><br />To honour her many literary works, she was appointed Commander of the Order of the British Empire in the 1956 New Year Honours. The next year, she became the President of the Detection Club. <br /><br /><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agatha_Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia entry for Agatha Christie</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12359988023329765706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Yes, but for my quick eyes, the eyes of a cat, Hercule Poirot might now be crushed out of existence - a terrible calamity for the world. And you, too, mon ami - though that would not be such a national catastrophe."<br /> "Thank you," I said coldly.&rdquo;</span>
